## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics (nonlinear dynamics and oscillations)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration and the features are position x, velocity v, and time t, which is the standard state-space form of a (possibly driven/damped) nonlinear oscillator. Common relationships express dv_dt as a restoring-force term depending on x (linear/nonlinear), plus damping depending on v, plus optional external forcing depending on t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Undamped linear oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x (simple harmonic restoring acceleration)
- Viscously damped linear oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (mass-normalized spring-damper)
- Constant-force bias: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 (equilibrium shifted by constant load)
- Sinusoidally forced oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (external periodic driving)
- Phase-shifted forcing: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4) (driving with phase)
- Duffing (hardening/softening spring): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (cubic stiffness nonlinearity)
- Duffing with forcing: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (canonical driven Duffing)
- Nonlinear (quadratic) damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * v * Abs(v) (drag-like dissipation)
- Nonlinear (cubic) damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * v**3 (amplitude-dependent damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (1 - c1 * x**2) * v - c2 * x (negative damping at small |x|, limit cycle)
- Pendulum small-to-large angle model: dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) - c2 * v (sinusoidal restoring torque with damping)
- Piecewise/hardening restoring force: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x * Abs(x) - c2 * v (non-smooth stiffness, e.g., geometric nonlinearity)
- Parametric stiffness modulation: dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (Mathieu-type parametric excitation)
- Time-varying damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - (c1 + c2 * cos(c3 * t)) * v (periodically modulated dissipation)
- Potential-gradient form (even potential): dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5) - c3 * v (restoring force from polynomial potential plus damping)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative oscillator signature: dv_dt depends mainly on x and is odd in x (e.g., -c*x, -c*sin(c*x)), with minimal v-dependence implying near energy conservation.
- Viscous damping: linear dependence on v (term -c*v) produces exponential decay of energy for small oscillations and is typical for linear friction models.
- Drag/turbulent damping: v*Abs(v) or v**3 terms indicate dissipation increasing strongly with speed, yielding faster decay at large amplitudes.
- Hardening vs softening stiffness: adding -c*x**3 shifts frequency with amplitude (positive cubic stiffness hardens, negative softens), a hallmark of Duffing-type behavior.
- Self-excited limit cycles: a factor like (1 - c*x**2)*v implies negative damping at small amplitude and positive damping at large amplitude, producing stable oscillations (Van der Pol mechanism).
- External periodic forcing: additive sin/cos(c*t) terms create resonance peaks and phase locking; multiple harmonics suggest non-sinusoidal driving.
- Parametric excitation: time-periodic coefficients multiplying x (or v) indicate Mathieu-like instability tongues and parametric resonance rather than direct forcing.
- Non-smooth mechanics: Abs(x), sign(x), or x*Abs(x) suggest piecewise stiffness/contact/backlash, often producing sharp corners in trajectories and higher harmonics.
- Symmetry clues: restoring terms typically odd in x; damping terms typically odd in v; violations (e.g., x**2 terms) may indicate bias, asymmetry, or coordinate offsets.

GT: -alpha*v**c0 - mu*(c1 - x**c2)*v - omega0**c3*x - omega0**c4*x*exp(-Abs(x))
Candidate formulas: 50

GT (fixed) is
\[
-0.0892421031789731\,v^3\;-\;0.725306435339938\,v(1-x^2)\;-\;1.44735630543929\,x\;-\;1.44735630543929\,x e^{-|x|}.
\]
Rewrite the middle term:
\[
-0.7253\,v(1-x^2)= -0.7253\,v + 0.7253\,v x^2.
\]
So GT consists of the basis functions:
- \(v^3\)
- \(v\)
- \(v x^2\)
- \(x\)
- \(x e^{-|x|}\)

Crucial: the \(x e^{-|x|}\) term is non-polynomial/non-rational in \(|x|\) and cannot be represented exactly by any finite combination of polynomials, \(|x|\)-polynomials, or rational functions in \(|x|\) like \(x/(c+|x|)^k\), nor by trig terms in \(t\), logs, Max, etc., unless the candidate explicitly contains \(e^{-|x|}\) (none do). Therefore every candidate can only match GT if it can somehow *exactly* reproduce \(x e^{-|x|}\), which they cannot. Below I still check each candidate’s available term types.

---

### Candidate 1
Polynomial in \(x\), \(v\), plus \(x|x|\), \(x|x|^3\), and \(x/(c+|x|)^3\). No \(e^{-|x|}\). Cannot match GT’s \(x e^{-|x|}\). **No match**.

### Candidate 2
Same as (1) but \(x|x|^4\). Still no exponential. **No match**.

### Candidate 3
Same structure; has \(x^5\) instead of \(x|x|^4\). No exponential. **No match**.

### Candidate 4
Has \(x/(c+|x|)^2\) and \(x^5\). No exponential. **No match**.

### Candidate 5
Has \(x/(c+|x|)^2\) and \(x|x|^5\). No exponential. **No match**.

### Candidate 6
Has \(x^7\) and \(x/(c+|x|)^3\). No exponential. **No match**.

### Candidate 7
Like (1) but two \(v^3\) coefficients; still no exponential. **No match**.

### Candidate 8
Like (1) without the last term; still no exponential. **No match**.

### Candidate 9
Linear terms in \(x\) (two coefficients), \(v\), \(vx^2\), \(v^3\), \(x/(c+|x|)^2\), \(x|x|\). No exponential. **No match**.

### Candidate 10
Like (4) without \(x^5\). No exponential. **No match**.

### Candidate 11
Has \(x^{c6}\) (power-law), \(x|x|\), \(x^5\), plus \(vx^2,v,v^3\). Power-laws cannot equal \(x e^{-|x|}\) for all real \(x\). **No match**.

### Candidate 12
Has \(x/(|x|+1)^3\) and \(x/(c9+|x|)^2\), plus polynomials. No exponential. **No match**.

### Candidate 13
Has \(x/(c6+x^2)^{1/3}\) (algebraic), plus polynomials. No exponential. **No match**.

### Candidate 14
Has \(x/(c8+x^2)\) rational in \(x^2\). No exponential. **No match**.

### Candidate 15
Same issue; no exponential. **No match**.

### Candidate 16
Has \(x\max(0,c9+|x|)\) (piecewise linear-ish) and \(x^{c6}\). No exponential. **No match**.

### Candidate 17
Only polynomials/power \(x^{c6}\) and \(x|x|\). No exponential. **No match**.

### Candidate 18
Like (12) but with \(x^5\) instead of second rational term. No exponential. **No match**.

### Candidate 19
Like (13) without \(x^5\). No exponential. **No match**.

### Candidate 20
Polynomials plus \(x/(c9+x^2)\) and an extra \(+v\). No exponential. **No match**.

### Candidate 21
Polynomials plus \(x/(c8+x^2)\). No exponential. **No match**.

### Candidate 22
Pure polynomial/\(|x|\)-polynomial terms. No exponential. **No match**.

### Candidate 23
Adds \(x\max(0,c9+|x|)\). Still no exponential. **No match**.

### Candidate 24
Adds \(x\max(0,c9+|x|)\) to the (12)-type set. Still no exponential. **No match**.

### Candidate 25
Adds \(v|v|\) and \(v|v||x|\). Still no exponential in \(x\). **No match**.

### Candidate 26
Adds \(v|v|\) and \(v^5\). Still no exponential. **No match**.

### Candidate 27
Adds \(v|v|\). Still no exponential. **No match**.

### Candidate 28
Same family; no exponential. **No match**.

### Candidate 29
Has \(x/(|x|+1)^3\), polynomials, and duplicated \(v\) terms. No exponential. **No match**.

### Candidate 30
Polynomials plus \(x^5\). No exponential. **No match**.

### Candidate 31
Polynomials plus \(x^5\). No exponential. **No match**.

### Candidate 32
Has \(x/(c6+x^2)^{1/3}\) and \(v/(c9+|v|)\). No exponential. **No match**.

### Candidate 33
Polynomials plus \(x^7\). No exponential. **No match**.

### Candidate 34
Adds \(v|v|^2 = v^3\) effectively (since \(|v|^2=v^2\)), but still no \(x e^{-|x|}\). **No match**.

### Candidate 35
Polynomials plus \(x^7\). No exponential. **No match**.

### Candidate 36
Adds \(x\sin(c8 t+c9)\). GT has no explicit \(t\)-dependence; to remove it set \(c7=0\). Still no exponential. **No match**.

### Candidate 37
Adds \(x\cos(c8 t)\) and \(v|v|\). Can set their coefficients to 0 to avoid extra terms, but still no exponential. **No match**.

### Candidate 38
Adds \(x\cos(c8 t)\); can set coefficient 0. Still no exponential. **No match**.

### Candidate 39
Adds \(v\cos(c8 t)\); can set coefficient 0. Still no exponential. **No match**.

### Candidate 40
Has \(v|v|\), \(v^{c8}\), \(v^3\). Even if tuned to match the \(v\)-side, still lacks \(x e^{-|x|}\). **No match**.

### Candidate 41
Has \(v/(c3+|v|)\) and polynomial terms. No exponential. **No match**.

### Candidate 42
Has \(|c3-x|\) and \(x|c3-x|\) (nonsmooth absolute kink at \(x=c3\)). GT’s \(x e^{-|x|}\) is smooth away from 0 and not representable by these. **No match**.

### Candidate 43
Has \(v|v|\) and \(v^{c8}\). Still no exponential. **No match**.

### Candidate 44
Adds \(v|v|\). Still no exponential. **No match**.

### Candidate 45
Only polynomial/\(|x|\)-polynomial in \(x\) and \(v\). No exponential. **No match**.

### Candidate 46
Polynomials only. No exponential. **No match**.

### Candidate 47
Has \(x^{c6}\), \(x^5\), \(x^7\). No exponential. **No match**.

### Candidate 48
Has algebraic \(x/(c6+x^2)^{1/3}\) plus \(x^5,x^7\). No exponential. **No match**.

### Candidate 49
Has \(\log(c7 e^{c8 v}+1)\) (a softplus-like function of \(v\)) and \(v|v|\). Still no \(e^{-|x|}\) term in \(x\). **No match**.

### Candidate 50
Has algebraic \(x/(c6+x^2)^{1/3}\) and \(x^5\). No exponential. **No match**.

---

Because none of the candidates contain an \(x e^{-|x|}\) (or any exponential in \(|x|\)) term, no choice of their free constants can make them exactly equal to the GT for all real \(x,v,t\) (with \(x,v\) allowed negative as stated).

[NO MATCH]

Conclusion: No match

GT Equivalence Verification (PO2)
============================================================
GT: -alpha*v**c0 - mu*(c1 - x**c2)*v - omega0**c3*x - omega0**c4*x*exp(-Abs(x))
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to determine which candidates can exactly match the Ground Truth (GT):

$$GT = -0.0892v^3 - 0.7253v(1 - x^2) - 1.4474x - 1.4474x\exp(-|x|)$$

Expanding:
$$GT = -0.0892v^3 + 0.7253vx^2 - 0.7253v - 1.4474x - 1.4474x\exp(-|x|)$$

So the GT has these basis functions:
1. $v^3$ 
2. $vx^2$
3. $v$
4. $x$
5. $x\exp(-|x|)$

The key challenge is matching $x\exp(-|x|)$. No candidate has an explicit $\exp(-|x|)$ term, so I need to check if any combination of terms in the candidates can represent $x\exp(-|x|)$.

**Taylor expansion of $x\exp(-|x|)$:** For $x > 0$: $xe^{-x} = x - x^2 + x^3/2 - x^4/6 + ...$, and for $x < 0$: $xe^{x} = x + x^2 + x^3/2 + x^4/6 + ...$. Note $x\exp(-|x|)$ is an odd function.

This means $x\exp(-|x|)$ cannot be exactly represented by any finite polynomial or rational function. Let me check each candidate's "extra" terms beyond the common $\{x, v, vx^2, v^3, x^3, x|x|\}$ basis.

**Common terms in most candidates:** $c_0 x + c_1 + c_2 vx^2 + c_3 v + c_4 x^3 + c_5 x|x| + c_6 v^3$

Note: $x|x|$ is $x^2\text{sgn}(x)$, which is odd but equals $x^2$ for $x>0$ and $-x^2$ for $x<0$. This is NOT the same as $xe^{-|x|}$.

The constant term $c_1$ must be 0 (GT has no constant). The $x^3$ and $x|x|$ terms are independent odd functions but cannot combine to give $xe^{-|x|}$.

**Key question:** Can any candidate's extra terms, combined with the common terms, exactly reproduce $xe^{-|x|}$?

Let me check candidates with rational terms like $x/(c + |x|)^n$:

For candidates with $x/(c_8 + |x|)^3$ (e.g., Candidate 8): Setting $c_8 = 1$, we get $x/(1+|x|)^3$. This is a rational function, NOT equal to $xe^{-|x|}$. No finite combination of polynomial and rational terms can equal $xe^{-|x|}$.

Similarly, $x/(c + x^2)^{1/3}$ (Candidates 13, 19, etc.) cannot match $xe^{-|x|}$.

$x\cos(ct)$, $x\sin(ct)$ — these depend on $t$, not $|x|$.

$x^{c_6}$ with free $c_6$ — this is a power function, not $xe^{-|x|}$.

$\log(c\exp(cv)+1)$ — softplus in $v$, irrelevant.

**None of these functional forms can exactly equal $xe^{-|x|}$.** The function $xe^{-|x|}$ is not a rational function, not a polynomial, not a power function, and not a trigonometric function. By linear independence of these function classes, no candidate can match.

Let me verify: every candidate lacks $xe^{-|x|}$ and has no exponential terms that could produce it. Therefore, no candidate matches.

Candidate 1 through 50 verdict: [NO MATCH] for all.
